file_answers('/opt/logicmoo_workspace/packs_sys/logicmoo_opencog/MeTTa/vspace-metta/examples/compat/metta-examples/SICP_book/chapter_1_3.metta', 17, [[]]).

;; Note: The following lambdaX type definition is more correct:
;; (: lambdaX (-> Variable Variable ... $t (-> $a $b ... $t)))
;; This definition also makes some additional examples work (see below).
;; But it doesn't prevent interpreter from evaluation of lambda's body
;; before lambda call is actually made. This is why Atom type
;; is used instead for the $body argument.
;; Note: The only reason why different definitions of lambdaX are needed is
;; that we would like to make lambda's interchangeable with other functions.
;; Otherwise we could define universal lambda like this:
;; (= ((lambda ; $vars $body) $vals) (let $vars $vals $body))
;; and use it like this:
;; (let $sum (lambda ($a $b $c) (+ (+ $a $b) $c)) ($sum (1 2 3))
;; quoted prevents wrapped atom from being interpreted
  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',:,quoted,[[->,'Atom','Atom']])
(: quoted 
  (-> Atom Atom))


;; Note: quoted is used in lambda implementations below to prevent $body to be
;; evaluated inside let.
;; Needed for putting lambda functions as input to functions
  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',:,lambda1,[[->,'Variable','Atom',[->,A,T]]])
(: lambda1 
  (-> Variable Atom 
    (-> $A $T)))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[[lambda1,Var,Body],Val],[let,[quoted,Var],[quoted,Val],Body])
(= 
  ( (lambda1 $Var $Body) $Val) 
  (let 
    (quoted $Var) 
    (quoted $Val) $Body))


;; For lambda without any input
  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',:,lambda0,[[->,'Atom',[->,T]]])
(: lambda0 
  (-> Atom 
    (-> $T)))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[[lambda0,Body]],Body)
(= 
  ( (lambda0 $Body)) $Body)


;; For lambda with two inputs
  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',:,lambda2,[[->,'Variable','Variable','Atom',[->,A,B,T]]])
(: lambda2 
  (-> Variable Variable Atom 
    (-> $A $B $T)))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[[lambda2,Var1,Var2,Body],Val1,Val2],[let,[quoted,[Var1,Var2]],[quoted,[Val1,Val2]],Body])
(= 
  ( (lambda2 $Var1 $Var2 $Body) $Val1 $Val2) 
  (let 
    (quoted 
      ($Var1 $Var2)) 
    (quoted 
      ($Val1 $Val2)) $Body))


;; For lambda with three inputs. But actually we will use it to bypass recursive limitation while
;; defining function using let
  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',:,lambda3,[[->,'Variable','Variable','Variable','Atom',[->,A,B,C,T]]])
(: lambda3 
  (-> Variable Variable Variable Atom 
    (-> $A $B $C $T)))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[[lambda3,Var1,Var2,Var3,Body],Val1,Val2,Val3],[let,[quoted,[Var1,Var2,Var3]],[quoted,[Val1,Val2,Val3]],Body])
(= 
  ( (lambda3 $Var1 $Var2 $Var3 $Body) $Val1 $Val2 $Val3) 
  (let 
    (quoted 
      ($Var1 $Var2 $Var3)) 
    (quoted 
      ($Val1 $Val2 $Val3)) $Body))


;; Sum from $a to $b with pre-defined transition from $a to $(a+1) $next and function $term applied to $a
  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[sum,Term,A,Next,B],[if,[>,A,B],0,[+,[Term,A],[sum,Term,[Next,A],Next,B]]])
(= 
  (sum $Term $A $Next $B) 
  (if 
    (> $A $B) 0 
    (+ 
      ($Term $A) 
      (sum $Term 
        ($Next $A) $Next $B))))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[sqr,X],[*,X,X])
(= 
  (sqr $X) 
  (* $X $X))


;; Cube can't be defined as (* $x $x $x) as in Scheme
  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[cube,X],[*,X,[sqr,X]])
(= 
  (cube $X) 
  (* $X 
    (sqr $X)))


;; Convenient functions
  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[inc,X],[+,X,1])
(= 
  (inc $X) 
  (+ $X 1))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[dec,X],[-,X,1])
(= 
  (dec $X) 
  (- $X 1))


;; Sum all cubes values from $a to $b. Here $term is Cube and $next is just Inc
  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['sum-cubes',A,B],[sum,cube,A,inc,B])
(= 
  (sum-cubes $A $B) 
  (sum cube $A inc $B))


!(assertEqual 
  (sum-cubes 1 10) 3025)

[assertEqual,['sum-cubes',1,10],3025]

;; SICP-BOOK.CHAPTER-1-3.01

; 
; EVAL TEST
; took 95.55 milliseconds.
(loonit_success 
  (equal_enough_for_test  
    (3025) 
    (3025)))
; Evaluation took 97.23 milliseconds.
Deterministic: Empty

  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[identity,X],X)
(= 
  (identity $X) $X)


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['sum-integers',A,B],[sum,identity,A,inc,B])
(= 
  (sum-integers $A $B) 
  (sum identity $A inc $B))


!(assertEqual 
  (sum-integers 1 10) 55)

[assertEqual,['sum-integers',1,10],55]

;; SICP-BOOK.CHAPTER-1-3.02

; 
; EVAL TEST
; took 47.48 milliseconds.
(loonit_success 
  (equal_enough_for_test  
    (55) 
    (55)))
; Evaluation took 49.03 milliseconds.
Deterministic: Empty

  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['pi-sum',A,B],[sum,[lambda1,X,[/,1.0,[*,X,[+,X,2]]]],A,[lambda1,X,[+,X,4]],B])
(= 
  (pi-sum $A $B) 
  (sum 
    (lambda1 $X 
      ("/" 1.0 
        (* $X 
          (+ $X 2)))) $A 
    (lambda1 $X 
      (+ $X 4)) $B))


;; To get more precise pi-value we need more iterations (in SICP book 1000 is used). But metta is currently slower than
;; scheme so in sake of performance let ~3.10 be our pi-value
!(assertEqual 
  (* 8 
    (pi-sum 1 50)) 3.1031453128860114)

[assertEqual,[*,8,['pi-sum',1,50]],3.1031453128860114]

;; SICP-BOOK.CHAPTER-1-3.03

; 
; EVAL TEST
; took 43.10 milliseconds.
(loonit_failureR

        (pi-sum 1 50))) 
    (3.1031453128860114)))

;; Exercise 1.29.
;;
;; Simpson's Rule is a more accurate method of numerical integration than the method
;; illustrated above. Using Simpson's Rule, the integral of a function f between a and b is approximated as
;;
;; S|a,b of f =  h/3[y0 + 4y1 + 2y2 + 4y3 + 2y4 + ... + 2yn-2 + 4yn-1 + yn]
;;
;; where h = (b - a)/n, for some even integer n, and yk = f(a + kh).
;; (Increasing n increases the accuracy of the approximation.)
;; Define a procedure that takes as arguments f, a, b, and n and returns the value of the integral,
;; computed using Simpson's Rule. Use your procedure to integrate cube between 0 and 1
;; (with n = 100 and n = 1000), and compare the results to those of the integral procedure shown ab
  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[inc2,X],[+,X,2])
(= 
  (inc2 $X) 
  (+ $X 2))


;; Since metta currently doesn't support '+', '*' etc with 3+ parameters:
  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[4,A,B,C,D],[+,[+,A,B],[+,C,D]])
(= 
  (4 $A $B $C $D) 
  (+ 
    (+ $A $B) 
    (+ $C $D)))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['integral-simpson',F,A,B,N],[let,Func_h,[lambda0,[/,[-,B,A],N]],[let,Element_y,[lambda1,X,[F,[+,A,[*,X,[Func_h]]]]],[/,[*,[Func_h],[4,[Element_y,0],[Element_y,N],[*,4,[sum,Element_y,1,inc2,[-,N,1]]],[*,2,[sum,Element_y,2,inc2,[-,N,1]]]]],3]]])
(= 
  (integral-simpson $F $A $B $N) 
  (let $Func_h 
    (lambda0 
      ("/" 
        (- $B $A) $N)) 
    (let $Element_y 
      (lambda1 $X 
        ($F 
          (+ $A 
            (* $X 
              ($Func_h))))) 
      ("/" 
        (* 
          ($Func_h) 
          (4 
            ($Element_y 0) 
            ($Element_y $N) 
            (* 4 
              (sum $Element_y 1 inc2 
                (- $N 1))) 
            (* 2 
              (sum $Element_y 2 inc2 
                (- $N 1))))) 3))))


!(assertEqual 
  (integral-simpson cube 0 1 10) 0.25)

;; Exercise 1.30.
;;
;; The sum procedure above generates a linear recursion.
;; The procedure can be rewritten so that the sum is performed iteratively.
;; This variant unfortunately doesnt work since we're calling $iter inside its definition.
;;(= (sum-iter $term $a $next $b) (let $iter (lambda2 $a $result
;;                                        (if (> $a $b) $result ($iter ($next $a) (+ $result ($term $a)))))
;;                                        ($iter $a 0)))
;; and thus we will use lambda3 to bypass it
  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[isum,Term,A,Next,B],[let,Iter,[lambda3,Z,Result,Self,[if,[>,Z,B],Result,[Self,[Next,Z],[+,Result,[Term,Z]],Self]]],[Iter,A,0,Iter]])
(= 
  (isum $Term $A $Next $B) 
  (let $Iter 
    (lambda3 $Z $Result $Self 
      (if 
        (> $Z $B) $Result 
        ($Self 
          ($Next $Z) 
          (+ $Result 
            ($Term $Z)) $Self))) 
    ($Iter $A 0 $Iter)))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['isum-cubes',A,B],[isum,cube,A,inc,B])
(= 
  (isum-cubes $A $B) 
  (isum cube $A inc $B))


!(assertEqual 
  (sum-cubes 1 10) 
  (isum-cubes 1 10))

[assertEqual,['sum-cubes',1,10],['isum-cubes',1,10]]

;; Exercise 1.31
;;
;; a.  The sum procedure is only the simplest of a vast number of similar abstractions
;;     that can be captured as higher-order procedures. Write an analogous procedure
;;     called product that returns the product of the values of a function at points over
;;     a given range. Show how to define factorial in terms of product. Also use product
;;     to compute approximations to value of pi using the formula (by John Wallis).
;;
;;     pi   2 * 4 * 4 * 6 * 6 * 8 ...
;;     -- = -------------------------
;;     4    3 * 3 * 5 * 5 * 7 * 7 ...
;;
;; b.  If your product procedure generates a recursive process, write one that generates
;;     an iterative process. If it generates an iterative process, write one that generates
;;     a recursive process.
;; Recursive
  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[rproduct,Term,A,Next,B],[if,[>,A,B],1,[*,[Term,A],[rproduct,Term,[Next,A],Next,B]]])
(= 
  (rproduct $Term $A $Next $B) 
  (if 
    (> $A $B) 1 
    (* 
      ($Term $A) 
      (rproduct $Term 
        ($Next $A) $Next $B))))


;; Iterative
  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[iproduct,Term,A,Next,B],[let,Iter,[lambda3,Z,Result,Self,[if,[>,Z,B],Result,[Self,[Next,Z],[*,Result,[Term,Z]],Self]]],[Iter,A,1,Iter]])
(= 
  (iproduct $Term $A $Next $B) 
  (let $Iter 
    (lambda3 $Z $Result $Self 
      (if 
        (> $Z $B) $Result 
        ($Self 
          ($Next $Z) 
          (* $Result 
            ($Term $Z)) $Self))) 
    ($Iter $A 1 $Iter)))

;; -----------------------End of Exercise 1.31----------------------------
;; Exercise 1.32.
;;
;; a. Show that sum and product (exercise 1.31) are both special cases of a still
;;    more general notion called accumulate that combines a collection of terms,
;;    using some general accumulation function:
;;
;; (accumulate combiner null-value term a next b)
;;
;; Accumulate takes as arguments the same term and range specifications as sum and product,
;; together with a combiner procedure (of two arguments) that specifies how the current
;; term is to be combined with the accumulation of the preceding terms and a null-value
;; that specifies what base value to use when the terms run out. Write accumulate and show
;; how sum and product can both be defined as simple calls to accumulate.
;;
;; b. If your accumulate procedure generates a recursive process, write one that generates
;;    an iterative process. If it generates an iterative process, write one that generates
;;    a recursive process.
;; ----------------------------------
  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[raccumulate,Combiner,Null_value,Term,A,Next,B],[if,[>,A,B],Null_value,[Combiner,[Term,A],[raccumulate,Combiner,Null_value,Term,[Next,A],Next,B]]])
(= 
  (raccumulate $Combiner $Null_value $Term $A $Next $B) 
  (if 
    (> $A $B) $Null_value 
    ($Combiner 
      ($Term $A) 
      (raccumulate $Combiner $Null_value $Term 
        ($Next $A) $Next $B))))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[iaccumulate,Combiner,Null_value,Term,A,Next,B],[let,Iter,[lambda3,Z,Result,Self,[if,[>,Z,B],Result,[Self,[Next,Z],[Combiner,Result,[Term,Z]],Self]]],[Iter,A,Null_value,Iter]])
(= 
  (iaccumulate $Combiner $Null_value $Term $A $Next $B) 
  (let $Iter 
    (lambda3 $Z $Result $Self 
      (if 
        (> $Z $B) $Result 
        ($Self 
          ($Next $Z) 
          ($Combiner $Result 
            ($Term $Z)) $Self))) 
    ($Iter $A $Null_value $Iter)))


;; For test reasons of defined accumulate function:
  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['racc-sum',Term,A,Next,B],[raccumulate,+,0,Term,A,Next,B])
(= 
  (racc-sum $Term $A $Next $B) 
  (raccumulate + 0 $Term $A $Next $B))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['iacc-sum',Term,A,Next,B],[iaccumulate,+,0,Term,A,Next,B])
(= 
  (iacc-sum $Term $A $Next $B) 
  (iaccumulate + 0 $Term $A $Next $B))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['pi-raccsum',A,B],[let,Pi_term,[lambda1,X,[/,1.0,[*,X,[+,X,2]]]],[let,Pi_next,[lambda1,Y,[+,Y,4.0]],['racc-sum',Pi_term,A,Pi_next,B]]])
(= 
  (pi-raccsum $A $B) 
  (let $Pi_term 
    (lambda1 $X 
      ("/" 1.0 
        (* $X 
          (+ $X 2)))) 
    (let $Pi_next 
      (lambda1 $Y 
        (+ $Y 4.0)) 
      (racc-sum $Pi_term $A $Pi_next $B))))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['pi-iaccsum',A,B],[let,Pi_term,[lambda1,X,[/,1.0,[*,X,[+,X,2]]]],[let,Pi_next,[lambda1,Y,[+,Y,4.0]],['iacc-sum',Pi_term,A,Pi_next,B]]])
(= 
  (pi-iaccsum $A $B) 
  (let $Pi_term 
    (lambda1 $X 
      ("/" 1.0 
        (* $X 
          (+ $X 2)))) 
    (let $Pi_next 
      (lambda1 $Y 
        (+ $Y 4.0)) 
      (iacc-sum $Pi_term $A $Pi_next $B))))

;; -----------------------End of Exercise 1.32----------------------------
;; Exercise 1.33.
;;
;; You can obtain an even more general version of accumulate (exercise 1.32)
;; by introducing the notion of a filter on the terms to be combined. That is,
;; combine only those terms derived from values in the range that satisfy a
;; specified condition. The resulting filtered-accumulate abstraction takes
;; the same arguments as accumulate, together with an additional predicate of
;; one argument that specifies the filter. Write filtered-accumulate as a procedure.
;; Show how to express the following using filtered-accumulate:
;; a. the sum of the squares of the prime numbers in the interval a to b
;;    (assuming that you have a prime? predicate already written)
;; b. the product of all the positive integers less than n that are relatively prime
;;    to n (i.e., all positive integers i < n such that GCD(i,n) = 1).
  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['Abs',X],[if,[<,X,0],[*,X,-1],X])
(= 
  (Abs $X) 
  (if 
    (< $X 0) 
    (* $X -1) $X))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['Floor_',X],[if,[<,X,1],0,[inc,['Floor_',[dec,X]]]])
(= 
  (Floor_ $X) 
  (if 
    (< $X 1) 0 
    (inc 
      (Floor_ 
        (dec $X)))))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['Floor',X],[if,[<,X,0],[dec,[*,['Floor_',['Abs',X]],-1]],['Floor_',X]])
(= 
  (Floor $X) 
  (if 
    (< $X 0) 
    (dec 
      (* 
        (Floor_ 
          (Abs $X)) -1)) 
    (Floor_ $X)))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['Ceil',X],[if,[<,X,0],[*,['Floor_',['Abs',X]],-1],[inc,['Floor_',X]]])
(= 
  (Ceil $X) 
  (if 
    (< $X 0) 
    (* 
      (Floor_ 
        (Abs $X)) -1) 
    (inc 
      (Floor_ $X))))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[truncate,X],[if,[==,X,0],0,[if,[<,X,0],['Ceil',X],['Floor',X]]])
(= 
  (truncate $X) 
  (if 
    (== $X 0) 0 
    (if 
      (< $X 0) 
      (Ceil $X) 
      (Floor $X))))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[remainder,X,Y],[-,X,[*,Y,[truncate,[/,X,Y]]]])
(= 
  (remainder $X $Y) 
  (- $X 
    (* $Y 
      (truncate 
        ("/" $X $Y)))))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['smallest-divisor',N],['find-divisor',N,2])
(= 
  (smallest-divisor $N) 
  (find-divisor $N 2))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['find-divisor',N,Test_divisor],[if,[>,[sqr,Test_divisor],N],N,[if,['divides?',Test_divisor,N],Test_divisor,['find-divisor',N,[inc,Test_divisor]]]])
(= 
  (find-divisor $N $Test_divisor) 
  (if 
    (> 
      (sqr $Test_divisor) $N) $N 
    (if 
      (divides? $Test_divisor $N) $Test_divisor 
      (find-divisor $N 
        (inc $Test_divisor)))))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['divides?',A,B],[==,[remainder,B,A],0])
(= 
  (divides? $A $B) 
  (== 
    (remainder $B $A) 0))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['prime?',N],[==,N,['smallest-divisor',N]])
(= 
  (prime? $N) 
  (== $N 
    (smallest-divisor $N)))


;; Since $filter in filtered-accumulate could depend on two inputs, prime with two params is needed.
  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['prime?',N,B],['prime?',N])
(= 
  (prime? $N $B) 
  (prime? $N))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['filtered-accumulate',Filter,Combiner,Null_value,Term,A,Next,B],[if,[>,A,B],Null_value,[if,[Filter,A,B],[Combiner,[Term,A],['filtered-accumulate',Filter,Combiner,Null_value,Term,[Next,A],Next,B]],['filtered-accumulate',Filter,Combiner,Null_value,Term,[Next,A],Next,B]]])
(= 
  (filtered-accumulate $Filter $Combiner $Null_value $Term $A $Next $B) 
  (if 
    (> $A $B) $Null_value 
    (if 
      ($Filter $A $B) 
      ($Combiner 
        ($Term $A) 
        (filtered-accumulate $Filter $Combiner $Null_value $Term 
          ($Next $A) $Next $B)) 
      (filtered-accumulate $Filter $Combiner $Null_value $Term 
        ($Next $A) $Next $B))))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['prime-square-sum',A,B],['filtered-accumulate','prime?',+,0,sqr,A,inc,B])
(= 
  (prime-square-sum $A $B) 
  (filtered-accumulate prime? + 0 sqr $A inc $B))


!(assertEqual 
  (prime-square-sum 2 12) 208)

[assertEqual,['prime-square-sum',2,12],208]

  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[average,A,B],[/,[+,A,B],2])
(= 
  (average $A $B) 
  ("/" 
    (+ $A $B) 2))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['negative?',X],[<,X,0])
(= 
  (negative? $X) 
  (< $X 0))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['positive?',X],[>,X,0])
(= 
  (positive? $X) 
  (> $X 0))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[search,F,Neg_point,Pos_point],[let,Midpoint,[average,Neg_point,Pos_point],[if,['close-enough?',Neg_point,Pos_point],Midpoint,[let,Test_value,[F,Midpoint],[if,['positive?',Test_value],[search,F,Neg_point,Midpoint],[if,['negative?',Test_value],[search,F,Midpoint,Pos_point],Midpoint]]]]])
(= 
  (search $F $Neg_point $Pos_point) 
  (let $Midpoint 
    (average $Neg_point $Pos_point) 
    (if 
      (close-enough? $Neg_point $Pos_point) $Midpoint 
      (let $Test_value 
        ($F $Midpoint) 
        (if 
          (positive? $Test_value) 
          (search $F $Neg_point $Midpoint) 
          (if 
            (negative? $Test_value) 
            (search $F $Midpoint $Pos_point) $Midpoint))))))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['close-enough?',X,Y],[<,['Abs',[-,X,Y]],0.001])
(= 
  (close-enough? $X $Y) 
  (< 
    (Abs 
      (- $X $Y)) 0.001))


  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['half-interval-method',F,A,B],[let,A_value,[F,A],[let,B_value,[F,B],[if,[and,['negative?',A_value],['positive?',B_value]],[search,F,A,B],[if,[and,['negative?',B_value],['positive?',A_value]],[search,F,B,A],['Arguments','doesn\'t',have,different,signs]]]]])
(= 
  (half-interval-method $F $A $B) 
  (let $A_value 
    ($F $A) 
    (let $B_value 
      ($F $B) 
      (if 
        (and 
          (negative? $A_value) 
          (positive? $B_value)) 
        (search $F $A $B) 
        (if 
          (and 
            (negative? $B_value) 
            (positive? $A_value)) 
          (search $F $B $A) 
          (Arguments "doesn't" have different signs))))))

  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[tolerance],0.1)
(= 
  (tolerance) 0.1)


;; Here we had to switch places for $try and $close-enough local functions definitions (not like in SICP book)
;; or it just won't work
  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,['fixed-point',F,First_guess],[let,Try,[lambda2,Guess,Self_try,[let,Next,[F,Guess],[let,Close_enough_Q_,[lambda2,V1,V2,[<,['Abs',[-,V1,V2]],[tolerance]]],[if,[Close_enough_Q_,Guess,Next],Next,[Self_try,Next,Self_try]]]]],[Try,First_guess,Try]])
(= 
  (fixed-point $F $First_guess) 
  (let $Try 
    (lambda2 $Guess $Self_try 
      (let $Next 
        ($F $Guess) 
        (let $Close_enough_Q_ 
          (lambda2 $V1 $V2 
            (< 
              (Abs 
                (- $V1 $V2)) 
              (tolerance))) 
          (if 
            ($Close_enough_Q_ $Guess $Next) $Next 
            ($Self_try $Next $Self_try))))) 
    ($Try $First_guess $Try)))


;; FIXME: Requires correct lambda type to work (see note to the lambda2 definition above)
;;!(assertEqual
;;    (fixed-point sqr 0.5)
;;    0.00390625)
;; Sqrt approximation using fixed-point function
;;!(assertEqual
;;    (fixed-point (lambda1 $y (average $y (/ 2 $y))) 1.0)
;;    1.4166666666666665)
;; Exercise 1.35.
;;
;; Show that the golden ratio Phi (section 1.2.2) is a fixed point of the
;; transformation x ->  1 + 1/x, and use this fact to compute by means of the fixed-point procedure.
;; FIXME: Requires correct lambda type to work (see note to the lambda2 definition above)
;;!(assertEqual
;;    (fixed-point (lambda1 $x (+ 1 (/ 1 $x))) 1.0)
;;    1.6)
;; -----------------------End of Exercise 1.35----------------------------
;; Exercise 1.36.
;;
;; Modify fixed-point so that it prints the sequence of approximations
;; it generates, using the newline and display primitives shown in exercise 1.22.
;; Then find a solution to x^x = 1000 by finding a fixed point of x -> log(1000)/log(x).
;; (Use Scheme's primitive log procedure, which computes natural logarithms.)
;; Compare the number of steps this takes with and without average damping.
;; (Note that you cannot start fixed-point with a guess of 1, as this would cause division by log(1) = 0.)
;; Currently fixed-point is not working (see note above).
;; -----------------------End of Exercise 1.36----------------------------
;; Exercise 1.37.
;;
;; a) An infinite continued fraction is an expression of the form
;;
;;         N1
;; ---------------------
;;             N2
;; D1 +  ---------------
;;               N3
;;       D2 + ----------
;;             D3 + ....
;;
;; As an example, one can show that the infinite continued fraction
;; expansion with the Ni and the Di all equal to 1 produces 1/Phi, where Phi
;; is the golden ratio (described in section 1.2.2).
;; One way to approximate an infinite continued fraction is to truncate the
;; expansion after a given number of terms. Such a truncation, so-called k-term
;; finite continued fraction -- has the form
;;
;;         N1
;; ---------------------
;;             N2
;; D1 +  ---------------
;;               N3
;;       D2 + ----------
;;            .
;;             .
;;              .
;;                 Nk
;;                -----
;;                  Dk
;;
;;
;; Suppose that n and d are procedures of one argument (the term index i) that
;; return the Ni and Di of the terms of the continued fraction. Define a procedure
;; cont-frac such that evaluating (cont-frac n d k) computes the value of the k-term
;; finite continued fraction. Check your procedure by approximating 1/Phi using
;;
;; (cont-frac (lambda1 (i) 1.0)
;;            (lambda1 (i) 1.0)
;;            k)
;;
;; for successive values of k. How large must you make k in order to get an approximation
;; that is accurate to 4 decimal places?
;;
;; b) If your cont-frac procedure generates a recursive process, write one that generates an
;; iterative process. If it generates an iterative process, write one that generates a recursive process.
;; Recursive
  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[finite_continued_fraction,N,D,K],[let,Rec,[lambda2,I,Self,[if,[==,I,K],[/,[N,I],[D,I]],[/,[N,I],[+,[D,I],[Self,[inc,I],Self]]]]],[Rec,0,Rec]])
(= 
  (finite_continued_fraction $N $D $K) 
  (let $Rec 
    (lambda2 $I $Self 
      (if 
        (== $I $K) 
        ("/" 
          ($N $I) 
          ($D $I)) 
        ("/" 
          ($N $I) 
          (+ 
            ($D $I) 
            ($Self 
              (inc $I) $Self))))) 
    ($Rec 0 $Rec)))

  ; Action: load=metta_atom('&self',=,[ifinite_continued_fraction,N,D,K],[let,Iter,[lambda3,A,Result,Self_iter,[if,[==,A,0],[/,[N,A],[+,[D,A],Result]],[if,[==,A,K],[Self_iter,[dec,A],[/,[N,A],[D,A]],Self_iter],[Self_iter,[dec,A],[/,[N,A],[+,[D,A],Result]],Self_iter]]]],[Iter,K,0,Iter]])
(= 
  (ifinite_continued_fraction $N $D $K) 
  (let $Iter 
    (lambda3 $A $Result $Self_iter 
      (if 
        (== $A 0) 
        ("/" 
          ($N $A) 
          (+ 
            ($D $A) $Result)) 
        (if 
          (== $A $K)

            (dec $A) 
            ("/" 
              ($N $A) 
              ($D $A)) $Self_iter) 
          ($Self_iter 
            (dec $A) 
            ("/" 
              ($N $A) 
              (+ 
                ($D $A) $Result)) $Self_iter)))) 
    ($Iter $K 0 $Iter)))
